Therefore the mind in conjunction. with the body is the patra and the enjoyment of the world (vishayanubhava) is the Amс╣Ыta. The patra is the Suryamandala and the Amс╣Ыta is Chandramandala. Jiva is able outside look. The Amс╣Ыta for the Jiva is the Ihamutr─Бrthaphalabhoga or the enjoyment of fruits here and elsewhere. Its nature is partly pleasure and partly pain, For the enjoyment of these, the mind is essential. But such enjoyment stands on a different footing from the pleasures cognised by the senses. While these latter are enjoyed as the result of ordinary modifications of the mind, the former is experienced only by the illumination of the witness-consciousness. For it is the mind itself that has undergone transformation into pleasure and pain and there is no other enjoyment of objects of sense. It is thus clear that the mind alone is the Amс╣Ыta enjoyed by the Jiva. That

110 ┼ЪR─кVIDYASAPARY─АV─АSAN─А the mind is the Chandramandala is stated from the standpoint of Adhidevata; for, according to the Sastras, Chandra or the moon is the Adhidevat─Б (presiding deity) of manas, which is a functional division of the antahkarana. This moon is the bhutachandra who resides in the Vi┼Ыuddhichakra with the sixteen petals. The influence of this Chandramandala extends as far as the Aj├▒─Бchakra. Here is experienced the feeling of pleasure and pain.. Is not the removal of this Jivabhava which is responsible for the Jiva feeling that he is an enjoyer of pleasure and pain, the prime goal of this J├▒anayaga, namely, the worship of Paradevat─Б? Therefore, one should attempt to get over the enjoyment of the Amс╣Ыta given out by the reflected Chandramandala that is ever-changing and attain the Ananda which is the Amс╣Ыta of the never-changing Chit Chandra. The experience of this ananda also takes place in the Aj├▒a chakra. That the mind which is predominant in suddha satva and which is able to see everything as an undivided whole is the Amс╣Ыta or the experience of ananda is the most esoteric and irrefutable conclusion. If the Jiva should get over the experience of pleasure and pain, the sense of differentiation due to the triputi should vanish. If this should vanish,

KHANDA IV 111 the sensing of name and form should disappear. For the disappearance of name and form, the feeling of undifferentiated continuity (akhandakaravс╣Ыtti) should set in. This continuity of experience of Satchidananda is the Amс╣Ыta. This is imperishable and never-ceasing ananda. 114 SR─кVIDYASAPARY─АV─АSAN─А oneness will arise. Therefore the piece indicates the Jiva who is fully endowed with all sadhanas, viz., discrimination, desirelessness etc. The pronunciation of the matс╣Ыk─Бs in the right order and the reverse order, suggests manana and nididhy─Бsana which are required to get over asambh─Бvan─Б and viparitabhavana (non-comprehension and misconstruction). Ashс╣нagandhalolitapushpa (the flower with the eight sweet scents):-These scents stand for the eight sadhanas-viveka, vair─Бgya, sama, dama, uparati, titiksha, ┼Ыraddha and sam─Бdh─Бna. When these eight are well established, the existence of mumukshutva is assured. This mumukshutva is the pushpa. If a mumukshu should cross the ocean of samsara, he should plunge in the nectar of the union of Jiva and Brahman. Therefore the throwing in of the flower with the eight scents suggests that a mumukshu possessing all the necessary sadhanas should always have akhaс╣Зс╕Н─Бk─Бravrtti. -This mantra is then recited. This is the Mс╣Ыtyunjaya mantra and indicates that it is only by conquering Mс╣Ыtyu (death) that amс╣Ыta (immortality) can be obtained.

The meaning of the refrain : is “I am not a Jiva (but Siva who is not different from the Chitsakti that is Satchitananda). " If this state should be obtained, the Jivabhava should be sacrificed in the sacred fire of knowledge. It is only when the Jivabh─Бva is brushed aside that

118 SRIVIDYASAPARYAVASAN─А Ananda will make itself felt. Therefore the Sastras declare that Tarpana (libation) is the indicator of Ananda. The highest significance of the refrain is the cutting down of all the limiting adjuncts of the Jiva by the sword of knowledge. The Amс╣Ыtakala┼Ыa which the Sudhadevi holds in one of her hands and the flesh of the fish in the other, respectively stand for Moksha or eternal bliss and the transient pleasures of the world. The fish is suggestive of an impure mind. It is in such a mind that the Jivabhava shows its illusory appearance. This is Pravс╣Ыtti marga and the other, the Nivс╣Ыtti marga. In both these paths, Siva. who is Ananda is ever present, but in Pravс╣Ыtti marga the deluded Jiva thinks that the Ananda. which is really that of the soul is derived from external sources and makes all possible attempts to secure such sensual pleasures. The happinessthus obtained is transient, but when these upa-dhis that are the tools in the enjoyment are removed, the same vishayasukha becomes nirup─Б.. dhikasukha. This is Nivс╣Ыtti marga. The sensual pleasures consist of sound, touch, form, taste and smell which are sensed by the five J├▒anendriyas. These constitute the world of enjoyment. These are the subtler forms of the fiveelements and it is these that are termed the five mak─Бras in the Sakta Tantras. or Here the

120 ┼ЪRIVIDYASAPARY─АV─АSAN─А The Tantras call these “Kuladravyas” also,’ Kula” being the collective name for the six chakras from Muladhara to Aj├▒a, which, as stated on page 84, are the seats of the five elements and the mind which cognises them. These Kuladravyas are the indicators of Brahman which is Ananda. рдЖрдирдиреНрджрдВ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордгреЛ рд░реВрдкрдВ рддрдЪреНрдЪ рджреЗрд╣реЗ рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╕реНрдерд┐рддрдореН ред рддрд╕реНрдпрд╛рднрд┐рд╡реНрдпрдЮреНрдЬрдХрд╛рдГ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрдордХрд╛рд░рд╛рдГ рдХреБрд▓рд╕рдВрдЬреНрдЮрд┐рдХрд╛рдГ рее (Kul─Бrnava). Some Tantras, however, enumerate these Kuladravyas as consisting of the five-madya, matsya, m─Бс╣Бsa, mudra and maithuna-for the sake of adhamadhikari┼Ы. Such Tantras have as their goal the Karmakanda and not the J├▒anak─Бс╣Зс╕Нa. For instance, a text of Kularс╣Зava says:- рдпрдерд╛ рдХреНрд░рддреБрд╖реБ рд╡рд┐рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рд╕реЛрдордкрд╛рдирдВ рд╡рд┐рдзреАрдпрддреЗ рдорджреНрдпрдкрд╛рдирдВ рддрдерд╛ рдХрд╛рд░реНрдпрдВ рд╕рдордпреЗ рднреЛрдЧрдореЛрдХреНрд╖рджрдореН || ред рее (V. 90). As the Deviyaga is therein likened to a sacrifice with external accessories, it is clear that it is included in the Karmakanda and as such is meant only for the adhamadhikari. With the uttamadhikari, however, this yaga is a J├▒anayaga out and out and there is no need for any external accessories. The very Tantras that prescribe the Pa├▒chamak─Бras as the Kuladravyas in the case of the

KHANDA IV 121 adhamadhikari declare their true significance for the benefit of the uttam─Бdhikari as shown below. There is no need to dilate further on this topic. It is impossible, however, to purify objects intrinsically impure. Therefore, in order to admit of purification, the idea of impurity should have been due to a delusion. The narrative in the Mahabharata that Karna who was for long immensely grieved under the delusion that he was. of a low birth became happy, once the conviction of his true Kshattriya descent set in, deserves to be borne in mind in this connection. Although by the application of bhagaty─Бgalakshaс╣З─Б (partially exclusive second. ary sense), avidya has disappeared and along with it, j─лvabhava, the association of objects and senses will continue till the Jiva’s prarabdha exists, so that not only will the mind sense the objects but there will also be the resultant enjoyments. рдирд┐рддреНрдпрдВ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдо рдирд┐рд░рдиреНрддрд░рдВ рд╡рд┐рдореГрд╢рддрд╛ рдирд┐рд░реНрд╡реНрдпрд╛рдЬрд╢рд╛рдиреНрддрд╛рддреНрдордирд╛ рднреВрддрдВ рднрд╛рд╡рд┐ рдЪ рджреБрд╖реНрдХреГрддрдВ рдкреНрд░рджрд╣рддрд╛ рд╕рдВрд╡рд┐рдиреНрдордпреЗ рдкрд╛рд╡рдХреЗ ред рдкреНрд░рд╛рд░рдмреНрдзрд╛рдп рд╕рдорд░реНрдкрд┐рддрдВ рд╕реНрд╡рд╡рдкреБрд░рд┐рддреНрдпреЗрд╖рд╛ рдордиреАрд╖рд╛ рдордо (Manish─Бpa├▒chaka) The assignment of these to the sthula, s┼лkshma and k─Бrana sar─лras is the Bali (sacrifice). KHANDA IV 131 Dipini Mantra. It runs thus: рдРрдВ рд╡рдж рд╡рдж рд╡рд╛рдЧреНрд╡рд╛рджрд┐рдирд┐ рдРрдВ; рдХреНрд▓реАрдВ рдХреНрд▓рд┐рдиреНрдиреЗ рдХреНрд▓реЗрджрд┐рдирд┐ рдХреНрд▓реЗрджрдп рдорд╣рд╛рдХреНрд╖реЛрднрдВ рдХреБрд░реБ рдХреБрд░реБ рдХреНрд▓реАрдВ ; рд╕реМрдГ рдореЛрдХреНрд╖рдВ рдХреБрд░реБ рдХреБрд░реБ ; рд╣реНрд╕реМрдГ рд╕реНрд╣реМрдГ ред That modification of the mind that reveals the Pratyag─Бtman is known as Dipin─лvс╣Ыtti and the mantra that produces it is the Dipini mantra. It is made up of three khandas with the bijas of Vagbhava, Kamaraja and Sakti k┼лtas respectively and has the Prasadapara and the Parapr─Бs─Бda b─лjas affixed at the end. The import of this mantra is explained by the learned as follows:-The Vagbhavakhanda defines the purport of the Vedas and Sastras as the Pratyag─Бtman which is in no way different from Brahman. The Kamarajakhaс╣Зс╕Нa suggests that to realise such Atman the mind should become pure and fluid as amс╣Ыta. This is the state known as “Atmagochara akhaс╣Зс╕Н─Бk─Бravс╣Ыtti.” The Saktikhanс╕Нa says that by the above state of mind one attains moksha. The Prasadapara and the Parapr─Бs─Бda bijas suggest the unity of Jiva and Brahman and the state of Jivanmukti. Guruyajana. AAZ KHANDA IV Atmap─Бtrasvik─Бra. (33) 133 This stands for nididhyasana. The upasaka should first contemplate on the Chidagni maс╣Зс╕Нala which has for its background the Kundalini sakti in the Muladhara, which is as slender as the awn of a niv─Бra grain and which is kept burning by the fuel of impressions of past deeds. He should then consider it to be his true self and sacrifice in it the punya, papa, kс╣Ыtya, akс╣Ыtya, samkalpa, vikalpa, dharma and adharma accumulated by him in his previous births; i.e., he should feel that none of these have anything to do with him who is the Pratyag─Бtman, and that they are really no part of him. The Chidagni destroys all karma. By such a nididhyasana, all karmas done in the past by the Jiva as a result of his association with prana, buddhi and body, during the three states of waking, dreaming and deep sleep, by thought, word and deed are dedicated to Brahman and therefore they disappear without leaving any trace. The way nididhyasana should be carried out is as follows:-. рдЖрд░реНрджреНрд░ рдЬреНрд╡рд▓рддрд┐ рдЬреНрдпреЛрддрд┐рд░рд╣рдорд╕реНрдорд┐ рдЬреНрдпреЛрддрд┐рдЬреНрд╡рд▓рддрд┐ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдорд╛рд╣рдорд╕реНрдорд┐ ред рдпреЛрд╜рд╣рдорд╕реНрдорд┐ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдорд╛рд╣рдорд╕реНрдорд┐ рдЕрд╣рдорд╕реНрдорд┐ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдорд╛рд╣рдорд╕реНрдорд┐ ред рдЕрд╣рдореЗрд╡рд╛рд╣рдВ рдорд╛рдВ рдЬреБрд╣реЛрдорд┐ рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рд╣рд╛ ||

134 SRIVIDYASAPARYAVASAN─А “This Visesharghya is the Chaitanya that is in me. That chaitanya is self-effulgent. This effulgence which is Brahman is myself. The Jivabhava has been imposed on my true self. This is due to aj├▒─Бna and when such aj├▒─Бna is removed by J├▒ana, the Brahmabhava that is already there shows forth. Brahmabh─Бva is not created afresh. I was Brahman before, I am Brahman now and I shall be Brahman always. I am uniting with my self what is in this patra removing the super-imposed visible form.” With such thoughts should the upasaka take the Atmapatra. Resum├й OF KHANDA IV. Patra. KHANDA V, From Antaryaga to Layangap┼лj─Б. (9-) The following topics are dealt with in this Khanda: (i) Antary─Бg─Б-Murtikalpana and dhyana- Ten mudras (ii) Avahana (iii) Chatushshashtyupach─Бrap┼лj─Б (iv) Chatur─Бyatanap┼лj─Б i.e., worship of Gana- pati, Surya, Vishnu and Siva. (v) Layangap┼лj─Б (vi) Shadang─Бrchana (vii) Nityadeviyajana (viii) Gurumandalarchana. (i) Antary─Бga. (9-2) Antaryaga or Antarapuja is internal or mental worship. This is of two kinds viz., Sadh─Бr─Б or with support and Niradhara or without support. рдкреВрдЬрд╛ рдпрд╛рднреНрдпрдиреНрддрд░рд╛ рд╕рд╛рдкрд┐ рджреНрд╡рд┐рд╡рд┐рдзрд╛ рдкрд░рд┐рдХреАрд░реНрддрд┐рддрд╛ ред рд╕рд╛рдзрд╛рд░рд╛ рдЪ рдирд┐рд░рд╛рдзрд╛рд░рд╛ рдирд┐рд░рд╛рдзрд╛рд░рд╛ рдорд╣рддреНрддрд░рд╛ рее рд╕рд╛рдзрд╛рд░рд╛ рдпрд╛ рддреБ рд╕рд╛рдзрд╛рд░реЗ рдирд┐рд░рд╛рдзрд╛рд░рд╛ рддреБ рд╕рдВрд╡рд┐рджрд┐ ред рдЖрдзрд╛рд░реЗ рд╡рд░реНрдгрд╕рдВрдХреврдкреНрддрд╡рд┐рдЧреНрд░рд╣реЗ рдкрд░рдореЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░реАрдореН ||

136 ┼ЪRIVIDYASAPARYAVASANA рдЖрд░рд╛рдзрдпреЗрджрддрд┐рдкреНрд░реАрддреНрдпрд╛ рдЧреБрд░реБрдгреЛрдХреНрддреЗрди рд╡рд░реНрддреНрдордирд╛ ред рдпрд╛ рдкреВрдЬрд╛ рд╕рдВрд╡рд┐рджрд┐ рдкреНрд░реЛрдХреНрддрд╛ рд╕рд╛ рддреБ рддрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдВ рдордиреЛрд▓рдпрдГ рее рд╕рдВрд╡рд┐рджреЗрд╡ рдкрд░рд╛рд╢рдХреНрддрд┐рд░реНрдиреЗрддрд░рд╛ рдкрд░рдорд╛рд░реНрдерддрдГ ред рдЕрддрдГ рд╕рдВрд╡рд┐рджрд┐ рддрд╛рдВ рдирд┐рддреНрдпрдВ рдкреВрдЬрдпреЗрдиреНрдорддрд┐рдорддреНрддрдордГ || (S┼лtasamhita. I. v. 11-14) Sadh─Бra Antarapuja consists in imagining an image or Chakra, invoking the Chit┼Ыakti therein. and worshipping it with imaginary offerings etc. Nir─Бdh─Бra ─Бntarap┼лj─Б, on the other hand, consists in contemplating on pure Satchidananda without imagining any objects for the mind to rest upon. This second kind is certainly superior, but the first is the necessary training ground for it and is therefore dealt with in the Paddhati. Bahiryaga without Antaryaga is decidedly avaidika (not countenanced by the Vedas). Antaryaga demands a proper contemplation of one’s Atman first in one’s own mind and then a perception of the Atman in the external world also. producing thereby an idea of non-differentiation between them. The ┼Ъruti text-is-ai aag┬╢├а a textтАФрдпреЛрд╜рдиреНрдпрд╛рдВ рджреЗрд╡рддрд╛рдореБрдкрд╛рд╕реНрддреЗ рди рд╕ рд╡реЗрдж ред “he who worships the Deity as distinct from him does not know,” has reference to the worship of images which involves a feeling of difference between the deity and the worshipper. Therefore Antaryaga is very essential while as for Bahiryaga, the Sastras go to the extent of saying that it is not necessary at all for the uttam─Бdhikari. Murtikalpana:-That one’s body, mind and world of enjoyment are super-imposed by one’s own mistaken imagination on the Chit┼Ыakti, which is the connotation of the Ahampada, is the settled conclusion of all the Sastras. It is necessary there. fore that the Sri Chakra which is suggestive of the Chitsakti, should be considered to be the world,

The Sakta Sastras assert that all Devas are rays of Chitsakti. Therefore to view the four deities, Ganapati, Surya, Vishnu and Siva as the Chitsakti, the reality in the background after ignoring their names and forms, is the highest significance of the Chaturayatanap┼лj─Б. Note A. In this way to look at the Chit┼Ыakti, which is not different from the Atman or Brahman, behind the names and forms of all the Devas is known as Svapradhana upasti. Upasti or worship is of three kinds :-Svapradhana, Samapradhana and Asvapradhana. 1. The upasti that is performed after realising that the Brahman which is not different from

150 SRIVIDYASAPARYAVASAN─А the Atman is the important entity, ignoring names and forms, is known as Svapradhana upasti. This is meant for the uttamadhikari. This is also known as Par─Бp┼лj─Б. Bio 2. Samapradhana upasti is that worship where the super-imposed names and forms and the real background are considered of equal importance. This is meant for the madhyam─Бdhikari.. This is also known as Parapar─Бp┼лj─Б. 3. Asvapradhana upasti is that worship where the names and forms alone are considered important and the underlying reality entirely ignored. This is meant for the adhamadhikari. This is also known as Apar─Бp┼лj─Б. It is quite essential to recognise that in the Svapradhana upasti, although thirty-three crores of Devat─Бs or even more may be worshipped, the object of worship is only one, namely, Chitsakti and that ultimately this one too is not different from the upasaka. 152 ┼ЪRIVIDYASAPARY─АV─АSAN─А Vimar┼Ыa. It is very well known that the samarasya of ┼Ъiva and Sakti, or Prakasa and Vimarsa is Kamakala, the cause of the universe. The Kamakal─Б is the subtle aggregate of the Jagat, Jiva and Para. From it was formed the Trikoс╣Зachakra. This is the representation of Avyakta, Mahat and Ahankara tatvas. It is also the representation of Sabda which is of the nature of Pasyanti, Madhyama and Vaikhari. In fact whatever in this world are spoken of in sets of three were derived from this Trikona. The Ashс╣нakona which is the representation of the Puryashtaka was derived from the Trikona. In a similar way the five Vayus, Prana etc., and the five upavayus, Naga etc., along with their functions became the inner and outer Dasaras. The fourteen n─Бс╕Н─лs became the Manva┼Ыra. The functions of the five karmendriyas (talking etc.) and the tyaga, grahaka and upeksha buddhis together making eight, went to form the Ashс╣нadala padma. The five bh┼лtas, the five j├▒anendriyas, the five karmendriyas and the mind, making in all sixteen, formed the Shoс╕Нa┼Ыadala padma. Happiness and misery were not created by Isvara but are the creation of Jiva. This creation is like the appearance of the snake in the rope. Just as the illusory appearance of the snake vanishes by the true knowledge of the rope, so also the illusory ideas “I” and “mine,” and happiness and misery should disappear only on the advent of true knowledge.

154 ┼ЪRIVIDYASAPARY─АV─АSAN─А Such knowledge, known as Tatvaj├▒─Бna or Brahmavidya, comes by introspective analysis,. and this analysis is represented by the nine Chakras from Bhupura to Bindu. Is this not sufficient proof of the position that the Sri Chakra is only the mind responsible for the Jivasс╣Ыshti? Just as in the absence of investigation we consider this world of animates and inanimates as created by Isvara, so also is the statement that. the ┼Ъr─л Chakra represents the macrocosm and the microcosm made without due enquiry. On investigation, however, it is realised that the whole world is in reality all Chit, that the ideas of “I” and “mine” and happiness and misery, due to a feeling of separateness, are the Jiva’s own creation out of the three gunas of avidya and that themind is the primary cause for such illusion. рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдореИрд╡рд╛рд╣рдорд┐рджрдВ рдЬрдЧрдЪреНрдЪ рд╕рдХрд▓рдВ рдЪрд┐рдиреНрдорд╛рддреНрд░рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрддрд╛рд░рд┐рддрдВ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдВ рдЪреИрддрджрд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрдпрд╛ рддреНрд░рд┐рдЧреБрдгрдпрд╛ рд╕реЗрд╢рдВ рдордпрд╛ рдХрд▓реНрдкрд┐рддрдореН ред (Manish─Бpa├▒chaka). (iii) Shaddar┼Ыana Vidya (iv) Shaс╕Н─Бdh─Бra p┼лj─Б, (v) Amnayasamash╚Ыi p┼лj─Б. (vi) Dhupa, dipa etc. (i) Nav─Бvaraс╣Зa p┼лj─Б. (тВм3тИТ3) Introduction. It has been said before (p.153) that the ┼Ъr─л Chakra according to the Sс╣Ыshtikrama or order of evolution is made up of nine Chakras beginning with Bindu and ending with Bhupura and that it represents the macrocosm and the microcosm created by Parame┼Ыvara. But in worship it has been the practice to adopt the Samharakrama or order of involution and to consider the ┼Ъr─л Chakra as comprising of nine Avaranas (enclosures) beginning with Bhupura and ending with the Bindu Chakra. It has also been pointed out (p. 15) that in this worship the Sri Chakra is the mind with a predominance of suddhasatva, that each Chakra or Avarana represents a state of

160 SRIVIDYASAPARY─АV─АSAN─А the mind and that the Avaranadevat─Бs or ┼Ъaktis are modifications (vс╣Ыttis) of the mind. A detailed enquiry about these is undertaken in this Khanda. In the first Khanda while explaining the Pushpanjali to the Yoginis an idea as to what the Yoginis stand for was given (p.57). It is worth recalling what was said there, namely, that the nine categories of Yoginis all stand for the Chitsakti which forms the background of the several modifications etc., of the mind. The nine Chakras from Bhupura to Bindu represent the several states from Jagrat to Moksha of the Jiva. which are his own creation and form the suddha. and a┼Ыuddha samsara for him. The a┼Ыuddha. samsara is of the nature of bondage evolved by the impure mind while the suddha samsara is representative of the practice of J├▒ana to overcome such bondage with a mind that is predominant in satvaguna. In starting a detailed elucidation of what the Chakras represent, it is worth quoting the following lines from ┼Ъivadrshti :- рднреВрдкреБрд░рд╛рджрд┐рддреНрд░рд┐рднрд┐рд╢реНрдЪрддреНрд░реИрд░реНрд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рддреИрдЬрд╕рдкреНрд░рд╛рдЬреНрдЮрдпреЛрдГ ред рдзрд╛рдорддреНрд░рдпрдВ рд╡рд┐рднрд╛рд╡реНрдпрдВ рддрджреВрд░реНрдзреНрд╡реЗ рддрддреНрдкрджрдореИрд╢реНрд╡рд░рдореН рее рддрддреЛ рдмрд╣рд┐рд░реНрджрд╢рд╛рд░реЗ рддреБ рдЧреБрд░реВрдкрд╕рджрдирдВ рд╕реНрдореГрддрдореН ред рдЕрдиреНрддрд░реНрджрд╢рд╛рд░рдЪрдХреНрд░реЗ рддреБ рд╢реНрд░рд╡рдгрдВ рдЪ рд╡рд┐рднрд╛рд╡рдпреЗрддреН рее

KHANDA VI рд╡рд╕реБрдХреЛрдгреЗ рддреБ рдордирдирдВ рдирд┐рджрд┐рдзреНрдпрд╛рд╕рдВ рддреНрд░рд┐рдХреЛрдгрдХреЗ ред рдмрд┐рдиреНрджреМ рдд рд╢рд┐рд╡рдЬреАрд╡реИрдХреНрдпрдВ рднрд╛рд╡рдиреАрдпрдВ рдмреБрдзреИрдГ рд╕рджрд╛ рее рддреБ 161 “Wise men should consider the three Chakras Bhupura and Shoс╕Нa┼Ыadala and Ashtadala padmasas representing the three states of consciousness of the Jiva, namely Jagrat, Svapna and Sushupti, which are respectively presided over by Vi┼Ыva, Taijasa and Praj├▒a, the three special forms of Jiva. The Manva┼Ыra, the next of the Chakras, should be considered as Parame┼Ыvara, the cause of the universe, who is denoted by the word a in the mah─Бv─Бkya. They should consider the Bahirda┼Ы─Бra as the approach towards the Guru, the Antarda┼Ы─Бra as ┼Ыravana, the Ashс╣нakona as manana, the Trikona as nididhyasana and the Bindu as (savikalpa samadhi where there is) Jiva-Brahmaikya.” The first three Chakras representing the Jagrat, Svapna and Sushupti states, are common experience not only to mumukshus with pure hearts but also to the populace whose hearts are not so pure; for the ┼Ъri Chakra which is of the form of macrocosm and microcosm and which represents the antahkarana is meant for the Jivas to work out the karma that has accrued through the ages. The effects of past karma being reaped 11

162 ┼ЪR─кVIDY─АSAPARY─АV─АSAN─А in the three states, these have to be gone through by all individuals alike. These states are Aj├▒─Бna states. The Jiva reaps the effects of his past deeds in the waking and dreaming states and getting into deep sleep enjoys Brahmananda unconsciously for a while, but again relapses into those states as a result of the remaining karma. He thus passes through the three states, in regular order or otherwise, daily till death and is then re-born, when the same process is repeated over and over again. This is the verdict of the Sastras and the experience of all of us. While thus going round the cycle of births and deaths, an exceptional Jiva, by the influence of some good karma, yearning to get out of this rotation of Jagrat, Svapna and Sushupti, realises that there must be a Parame┼Ыvara who created him and the world and begins to enquire “What is the relation between me and Him? Where does He reside? and what is the relation between the world and Him?” and so on. The fourth Chakra represents the state of mind of such an individual who has just set his foot on the ascent to J├▒─Бna. Parame┼Ыvara alone is able to relieve the Jiva from samsara by removing his Aj├▒─Бna, and He is accordingly known as “Mochaka” or the Liberator. KHANDA VI рдЕрд╢реБрднрдХреНрд╖рдпрдХрд░реНрддрд╛рд░рдВ рдлрд▓рдореБрдХреНрддрд┐рдкреНрд░рджрд╛рдпрдХрдореН ред 163 рдпрджрд┐ рдпреЛрдиреНрдпрд╛рдГ рдкреНрд░рдореБрдЪреНрдпреЗрд╜рд╣рдВ рддрддреНрдкреНрд░рдкрджреНрдпреЗ рдорд╣реЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░рдореН | (Garbha Up.) But although one begins to think and find out the nature of Parame┼Ыvara, the Mochaka, it will be impossible to get a true knowledge of Him except through a Guru, who is therefore known as Mochakaprada or the giver of the Liberator. It thus becomes necessary for a mumukshu to get hold of a Guru to obtain a clear knowledge of Paramesvara and his relation with Him. The fifth Chakra is the mental attitude of such an earnest aspirant seeking and approaching a Guru. In this state of mind are included a recognition of the true nature of the Guru, the need of approaching him and the result of service to him. The sixth Chakra represents the mumukshu’s mind when he becomes the recipient of the Guru’s grace and his Mah─Бv─Бkyopade┼Ыa inculcating the unity of Jiva and Brahman, This is known as ┼Ыravana. Therefore the mental states saturated with Bhakti towards Isvara, Bhakti towards Guru and devout attention to his teachings are represented by the fourth, fifth and sixth Chakras respectively. The seventh, eighth and ninth Chakras represent the state of mind which has a predominance of suddha satva and which is immersed in manana, nididhyasana and savikalpa samadhi respectively.

164 SRIVIDYASAPARY─АV─АSAN─А Avaranas-General. Each Avaraс╣Зa or Chakra has a prakс╣Ыt├л (source), is of a different shape and goes by an appropriate name. Each has a Chakre┼Ыvari or presiding deity attended by her own retinue of Avaraс╣Зadevat─Бs or Yoginis with their parapher. nalia and is pervaded by a specific Siddhi and a Mudra. Each Avaranadevata has an individual name but all the devatas of an Avarana together have a distinctive group name of Yoginis (vide p. 57). The term Mudra has already been explained on p.142. Anything that conduces to knowledge or bliss is called by courtesy a Siddhi (accomplishment) on the analogy of the saying arg “ghee is (i.e., conduces to prolong) life.тАЭ The Puja of each Avarana comprises of the following items:-(1) Pushpanjali to the Chakra (2) Puja-tarpana of the Avaraс╣Зadevat─Бs (3) Pushpa├▒jali to the Yoginis (4) Puja-tarpana of the Chakreс╣гvari, Siddhi and Mudra (5) P┼лja-tarpana (thrice) of the Devi (6) Dhupa etc., upacharas (7) Bindutarpana or Dedication of the p┼лj─Б in the left hand of the Devi in the Bindu and (8) Prostration. The tabular statement attached gives particulars under several heads in respect of each Avarana. Explanations, esoteric significance etc., wherever necessary, will be given as each Avarana is taken up for consideration..

KHANDA VI First Avarana–Bhupura (3-4). The Prthv─лbija Chakra 165 which is the prakс╣Ыti of this should be taken as representative of all the five bh┼лtas (and their effects). This Chakra accordingly represents the Jagrada vasth─Б or waking state; for in this state, the gross body or annamayako┼Ыa, the senses and the mind, as also the sense-objects, together with the pleasures and pains arising from sense-contacts are all in full operation. The special Jiva (abhimani) of this state is known as Vi┼Ыva and described as Sthulabhuk or enjoyer of gross objects i.e., the external world. The full full sthula-triputi-knower, knowledge and known-functions primarily in this state, the prameya or the objective world playing the predominant part. Hence the names Tripurachakre┼Ыvari (Tripura tripu╚Ыi. ga ANAJE├Э agara afu) and Prakata yoginis (prakata-manifest or spread out).

Avaranadevat─Бs. There are three sets of Avarana-devat─Бs for this Chakra, one for each square. (i) Those of the first square are the ten SiddhisAnima, Laghima etc.,-which stand for the five objects of sense, the two excretory functions and the three categories of mental attitudes-Anukula (agreeableness), Pratikula (disagreeableness) and Upeksha (indifference).

166 SR─кVIDYASAPARY─АV─АSAN─А (ii) The Devatas for the second square are the eight M─Бtrs or Divine Mothers-Brahmi, Mahe┼Ыvari etc.,-who represent the eight dh─Бtus or essential ingredients (skin, blood, flesh, fat, bone, marrow, semen and strength) constituting the gross body or the abode of enjoyment for the Jiva. (iii) The Devat─Бs for the third square are the ten Mudras-Sarvasankshobhini, Sarvavidr─Бvin─л etc.,which are the embodiments of the worldly pleasures accruing during the enjoyment of the ten categories of objects etc., mentioned under the first square. The significance of Bindutarpana in the case of this Avarana is the firm recognition by the upasaka that the Chit┼Ыakti alone is the reality behind not only all the objects cognised in the waking state as separate from him but also of the mind which is the instrument of cognition and of the cogniser as well. Only if the triputi is destroyed. will the aspirant gain his end of final be-at-itude or Moksha. He should realise that the Prakatayoginis or the Chit┼Ыakti delimited by the gross heterogeneous objects of sense are but rays of the Paradevat─Б. Second Avarana-Shoс╕Нa┼Ыadalapadma (-) The Chandrabija being the prakrti of this Chakra, it should be taken to represent the mind

KHANDA VIV 167 which has Chandra for its Adhidevata and its modifications or the s┼лkshmatriputi. This Chakra therefore stands for the Svapnavasth─Б or dreaming state where the pramaс╣Зa, mind, is all-in-all. The seat of the mind in the dreaming state is the neck or the place of the moon, and this Chakra is only the sixteen-petalled lotus in the Vi┼Ыuddhi plexus in that region. It is called Sarv─Б┼Ы─Бparipuraka (i.e fulfilling all desires) Chakra, as whatever desiresetc., are left over in his waking state are experienced by the Jiva in the dreaming state. The special Jiva (abhimani) of this state is known as Taijasa and described as Praviviktabhuk or enjoyer of secret and subtle experiences (i.e., those composed of mere vasanas or impressions), in the subtle body constituted of the praс╣Зamaya, manomaya and vij├▒─Бnamaya ko┼Ыas. Hence the name Guptayoginis (gupta = secret) for the Chit┼Ыakti associated with this Chakra. The Avaranadevat─Бs for this Chakra are the sixteen Saktis–K─Бm─Бkarshiс╣З─л, Buddhy─Бkarshin─л etc. These are of the nature of mental modifications brought about by the movements of the mind and the pr─Бс╣Зa. рд╖реЛрдбрд╢рд╕реНрдкрдиреНрджрд╕рдВ рджреЛрд╣рдЪрдорддреНрдХреГрддрд┐рдордпреНрдпрдГ рдХрд╛рдорд╛рдХрд░реНрд╖рд┐рдгреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рдХрд▓рд╛- рд╢рдХреНрддрдпрдГ-рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд╛рджрд┐рдкрдЮреНрдЪрдХрдВ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд┐рдпрджрд╢рдХрдВ рдордирд╢реНрдЪреИрдХрдВ рдЖрд╣рддреНрдп рд╖реЛрдбрд╢ ред рдкрдерд╡рд╛ рдХреЗрд╡рд▓рдВ рдордирдГ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд╕реНрдкрдиреНрджрдиреЗрди рд╖реЛрдбрд╢рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░реЗрдг рдЪрд▓рдпрдиреН

168 ┼ЪRIVIDYASAPARY─АV─АSAN─А ред рд╡реГрддреНрддрд┐рд░реВрдкреЗрдг рдкрд░рд┐рдгрдорддрд┐ ред рддрд╛ рд╡реГрддреНрддрдп рдПрд╡ рд╕реНрд╡рдкреНрдиреЗ рдкрд░рд┐рджреГрд╢реНрдпрдорд╛рдирдкреНрд░рдкрдЮреНрдЪ рдЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рее (Yoginihс╣Ыdaya VIII Com). Third Avarana-Ashс╣нadalapadma (9-0) As the prakс╣Ыti of this Chakra is the Sivabija, the Mahapralaya which is the all-destroying function of Rudra is indicated. Of the three states enjoyed by the Jiva every day, Sushupti or deep sleep is of the nature of pralaya. The Sastras describe it as the Dinapralaya. In it prameya, the objective world and pramaс╣Зa, the cognising mind, are both dormant and pram─Бt─Б alone is active. Praj├▒a is the Jiva who is its abhim─Бni. He is Anandabhuk -the enjoyer of his own bliss-and is associated with the causal body or anandamayako┼Ыa. The eight ┼Ъaktis-Anangakusuma, Anangamekhal─Б etc., are the Devatas of this Avarana. They represent the s┼лkshma puryashс╣нakamade up of (1) Prakrti, (2) Mahattatva, (3) Ahamkara, (4) the pa├▒chatanm─Бtr─Бs, (5) the pa├▒chabh┼лtas, (6) the da┼Ыendriyas, (7) Antahkarana and (8) Purusha-which during deep sleep lies dormant in Aj├▒─Бna, its cause. Therefore, they are without bodies” (ananga) and “further hidden” (guptatara). Hence the names Anangakusum─Б etc and Guptatarayoginis given to the deities. 66

KHANDA VI 169 The Chakre┼Ыvari for this Avarana is called Tripurasundari, because She being self-resplendent shines forth through the three states and illuminates the objects of cognition in each; also because She affords relief to the Jiva done up after his worries during the Jagrat and Svapna states by giving him Sushupti in which to enjoy his inherent Ananda. рднреЛрдЧреНрдпрднреЛрдХреНрддреГрд░реВрдкрдкреНрд░рд╡реГрддреНрддреНрдпрд╛ рд╕рдВрдЬрдирд┐рддрд╢реНрд░рдордирд┐рд╡реГрддреНрддрд┐рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рдХ рд╕рд╣рдЬрд╛рди-рдиреНрджрд╛рд╡рд╛рдкреНрддрд┐рдГ рд╕реИрд╡ рд╕реМрдиреНрджрд░реНрдпрд╛рдЦреНрдпреЛ рдЧреБрдгрдГ ред рддреЗрди рд╕рдВрдпреБрддрд╛ рддреНрд░рд┐рдкреБрд░рд╕реБрдиреНрджрд░реА рдЪрдХреНрд░реЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░реА || (Yoginihс╣Ыdaya VIII.143. Amс╣Ыt─Бnanda’s com.) In Sushupti, the inherent Ananda is enjoyed along with Aj├▒ana when the inner and outer worlds, gross and subtle, are drawn in and absorbed in their cause. The experience “I had a blissful sleep but know nothing of what happened” is common to all. This feeling is represented by the Sarvakarshini (i.e drawing all) Mudra. The greatness (mahima) of Jiva lies in the fact that he is Praj├▒─Бnaghana or mass of intelligence and this is indicated by Mahimasiddhi. Note: Abhyasa or Avс╣Ыtti is the repeated meditation of Chit┼Ыakti which is Satchidananda, losing sight of the imaginary super-impositions, at every perception of the external world of name and form. Avс╣Ыtti is practically synonymous with Avarana

170 ┼ЪRIVIDYASAPARY─АV─АSAN─А or Avс╣Ыti (cover) as the need for Avrtti or repeated practice arises only because the object sought is shrouded. Should not repeated practice be made until the cover is removed? Just as a man, when his house is on fire, rushes out straightaway to a tank of water to save himself, not minding even his wife and children, so also an earnest aspirant, to save himself from samsaric afflictions, will forsake all desires and seek a Guru. рдЧреГрд╣реЗ рджрд╣реНрдпрдорд╛рдиреЗ рддрддреНрд░рд╕реНрдерджрд╣реНрдпрдорд╛рдирдГ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рдГ рдпрдерд╛ рдХрд▓рддреНрд░рдкреБрддреНрд░рд╛рджрд┐рдХрдВ рдкрд░рд┐рддреНрдпрдЬреНрдп рд╕реНрд╡рддрд╛рдкреЛрдкрд╢рдордирд╛рд░реНрдердореЗрд╡ рдмрд╣рд┐рд░реНрдирд┐рд░реНрдЧрддреНрдп рддрд╛рдкреЛрдкрд╢рдордирдВ рдХрд░реНрддреБрдорд┐ - рдЪреНрдЫрддрд┐, рдПрд╡рдВ рд╕рд╛рдВрд╕рд╛рд░рд┐рдХрддрд╛рдкреЛрдкрд╢рдордирдВ рд╕рдВрдкрд╛рджрдпрд┐рддреБрдВ рддреНрдпрдХреНрддрд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗрд╖рдгрдГ рд╕рдиреН рдореЛрдХреНрд╖реЗрдЪреНрдЫрдпрд╛ рд╕рджреНрдЧреБрд░реБрдВ рд╡реГрдгреЛрддрд┐ рее (Vasudevamanana)

180 ┼ЪR─кVIDYASAPARY─АV─АSAN─А Sixth Avarana-Antarda┼Ы─Бra (-) The preceding Avarana referred to the approach towards the Guru and service to him. Seventh Avarana-Ashс╣нakona (0-0) (ренрен-ренрео) An uttamadhikari, whose mind is free from obstacles to the direct realisation of Brahman, is able to feel “I am Brahman” the moment the Guru instructs him in the Mah─Бv─Бkya. In the case of others, however, the two defects of Asambhavana

184 ┼ЪRIVIDYASAPARYAVASAN─А or Samsaya (doubt) and Viparitabhavana (mis-comprehension) stand in the way of such an immediate realisation. These are the effects of the Abhana-padak─Бvaraс╣Зa part of Aj├▒─Бna or the notion that Brahman, though existing, is not perceived. Of these, the former i.e., Samsaya is got over by manana. Manana is the cogitation by means of reasoning, discussion etc., on the purport of the Mah─Бv─Бkyas as learnt from the Guru. рдЕрдкрд░реЛрдХреНрд╖рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдмрдиреНрдзрдХрд╛рднрд╛рдирд╛рд╡рд░рдгрдХреЛрд░реНрдпрднреВрддрд╛рд╕рдВрднрд╛рд╡рдирд╛рдирд┐ - рд╡реГрддреНрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердВ рдордирдирдВ рдХрд░реНрддрд╡реНрдпрдореН ред This Avarana accordingly represents manana. It is only in this Avarana that the special feature of Sri Vidya is brought out. ┼Ъr─л Vidya is Ahangrahopasana and is of the essence of manana, nididhy─Бsana and samadhi. If even after the initiation into the Mah─Бv─Бkya by the Guru, the disciple is not able to realise Brahman, the only inference is that doubts and counter-ideas obsess him. It is the accepted truth of the Sastras that these obsessions occur only to Akс╣Ыtopasakas i.e.. those who have not duly performed up─Бsan─Б. The removal of Abhanapadakavarana which thus impedes direct realisation is the supreme end of ┼Ъr─л Vidya upasana and it is the opinion of ┼Ъri Gaudapadacharya that such Akс╣Ыtopasakas should take to Sri Vidya for the attainment of direct realisation.

KHANDA VI 185 This idea of his is obtained from the opening sutra of his ┼Ъr─л Vidya Mantraratnas┼лtras, as already explained on pp.20-21. As this ─Аvarana is designed to root out Samsaya, it is necessary to know the nature of such samsaya. Samsaya is existence in the mind of several conflicting ideas about a given topic. рдПрдХрд╛рдзрд┐рдХрд░рдгреЗ рдкрд░рд╕реНрдкрд░рд╡рд┐рд░реБрджреНрдзрдирд╛рдирд╛рдзрд░реНрдордЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдореЗрд╡ рд╕рдВрд╢рдпрдГ ред This is of two kinds-Pramanagatasamsaya and Prameyagatasamsaya. Pramanagatasamsaya is the doubt whether all the Vedantic texts are authoritative or not with reference to the secondless ┼Ъiva. Prameyagatasamsaya is of two kinds :-Atmaprameyasamsaya and Anatmaprameyasamsaya. these, the latter is of countless varieties and a description of them is not of any use. Of Atmaprameyasamsaya is also of various kinds. as indicated below:- A-Regarding Atman as not distinct from Brahman: (1) Is ├Дtman different or not different from Brahman? (2) If it is not different, is it always so or only in Moksha? (3) If it is always not different, is it possessed of Ananda etc., or devoid of them?

186 SRIVIDYASAPARY─АV─АSAN─А (4) Although it is possessed of Ananda etc., are they qualities or do they inhere in it or form its Saktis? and so on. B-Regarding Atman itself: (1) Is Atman different from bodies etc. or not? (2) If it is different, is it microscopic, infinite or of medium size? (3) If infinite, is it a doer or non-doer? (4) If a non-doer, is it one or many with mutual differences? and so on. C-Regarding Isvara: (1) Is I┼Ыvara an embodied Being living in Kailasa or Vaikuntha, or not? (2) Although infinite and without a body, does He stand in need of atoms and the like for the creation of the universe or does He create it by His mere will? (3) Although not in need of anything for creation, is He only a creator pure and simple, or is He both efficient and material cause? (4) Although both efficient and material cause, is He the bestower of the fruits of the actions of Jivas or not? (5) Although the bestower of the fruits, is He tainted with the blemishes of injustice etc., or free from such faults? etc., etc.

KHANDA VI 187 By the samanvaya or harmonisation of all Vedantic texts, the Pramanagatasamsaya disappears and by the knowledge of their non-incongruity, the Prameyagatasamsaya vanishes. Therefore this seventh Avarana, which wipes out all Samsaya, is suggestive of the investigation of the entire Vedanta┼Ы─Бstra. This Chakra is known as Sarvarogahara (i.e., curer of all disease) as it radically cures the disease of samsara by dispelling all doubts in regard to the direct realisation of Siva. рдЕрдирд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рд╢реБрдЪрд┐ рдХреНрд▓реЗрд╢рд░реВрдкрд╕рдВрд╕рд╛рд░реЛ рд░реЛрдЧрдГ ред рддрд╕реНрдп рд╣рд░рдгреЗ рдкреНрд░рднрд╛рд╡- рд╢рд╛рд▓реАрддрд┐ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд░реЛрдЧрд╣рд░рдЪрдХреНрд░рдореН | The Yoginis of this Chakra are known as Rahasyayoginis. They represent the self-luminous undivided knowledge which is ultimately responsible for getting rid of samsara caused by the pursuit of duality. рд░рд╣рд╕реНрдпрдпреЛрдЧрд┐рдиреАрд░реНрджреЗрд╡рд┐ рд╕рдВрд╕рд╛рд░рджрд▓рдиреЛрдЬреНрдЬреНрд╡рд▓реЗ | рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд░реЛрдЧрд╣рд░реЗ рдЪрдХреНрд░реЗ рд╕рдВрд╕реНрдерд┐рддрд╛ рд╡реАрд░рд╡рдиреНрджрд┐рддреЗ ред (Y.Hr. viii.162). " Sarvakhecharimudra is that modification of the mind which, rid of all doubts, is able to feel the constant Brahmasvarupa. The Avaranadevatas of this Chakra are the modifications of the mind in the process of manana. They are of the form of ┼Ъruti texts as described below :—

() form also of The Paddhati prescribes the worship of the four Ayudhas or weapons of Kame┼Ыvara and Kame┼Ыvari, namely, bana, dhanus, p─Б┼Ыa and anku┼Ыa, in the west, north, east, and south respectively of the eighth Avarana and between it and the seventh Avaraс╣Зa.

190 ┼ЪRIVIDYASAPARY─АV─АSAN─А As the worship of these Ayudhas is to be performed after that of the seventh Chakra representing manana and before that of the eighth Chakra representing nididhyasana, it is apparent that the Ayudhas should signify the results of manana and the aids to nididhyasana. It has been pointed out above that as a consequence of manana, all doubts disappear. The mind, thus purified, begins to introspect and becomes fit for the direct realisation of the Atman. рд╡рд┐рд╢реБрджреНрдзрдмреБрджреНрдзреЗрдГ рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╡реЗрджрдирдВ рддреЗрдиреИрд╡ рд╕рдВрд╕рд╛рд░рд╕рдореВрд▓рдирд╛рд╢рдГ рее (Vivekach┼лс╕Н─Бmaс╣Зi 150).. The significance of the Ayudhas is given thus in the Lalita Sahasranama:-the kodanda is the mind, the pa├▒chabaс╣Зas are the five subtle elements,, p─Б┼Ыa is desire and anku┼Ыa is hatred. рдордиреЛрд░реВрдкреЗрдХреНрд╖реБрдХреЛрджрдгреНрдбрд╛ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрддрдиреНрдорд╛рддреНрд░рд╕рд╛рдпрдХрд╛ ред рд░рд╛рдЧрд╕реНрд╡рд░реВрдкрдкрд╛рд╢рд╛рдвреНрдпрд╛ рдХреНрд░реЛрдзрд╛рдХрд╛рд░рд╛рдЩреНрдХреБрд╢реЛрдЬреНрдЬреНрд╡рд▓рд╛ || If it should be asked how these are useful in the realisation of the Atman, the answer is as follows: The five subtle elements stand for the five J├▒anendriyas. If these are properly controlled. and made to merge in the mind, it can be prevented from looking outwardly and turned inwards. It can then be made to develop an intense interest in the realisation of the Atman and an utter dislike

KHANDA VI 191 for the objective world. What doubt is there then that these Ayudhas which represent the state of such a mind, are aids to Atmaj├▒─Бna? Another explanation is also possible. The four Ayudhas may be said to be the removers of laya, vikshepa, kashaya and ras─Бsv─Бda, the four obstacles in the way to nididhyasana and samadhi. Thus:-

  1. P─Б┼Ыa removes the obstacle kashaya or confusion. The intense desire to realise ├Гtman at any cost is p─Б┼Ыa. By this, ideas of anatman which constitute kashaya are ruled out.
  2. Anku┼Ыa removes the obstacle laya or sleep.. Anku┼Ыa is a dislike for the anatman which is made up of names and forms.
  3. Dhanus removes vikshepa or perturbation. Dhanus is the pure mind turned inwards. As there is no external activity to the pure mind, imaginations that make up vikshepa do not arise. or
  4. Pa├▒chab─Бс╣Зas remove the obstacle rasasv─Бda infatuation. Pa├▒chab─Бnas stand for Jitendriyatva. The five J├▒anendriyas when they are turned away from their vishayas, sabda etc., merge in the mind and there is no scope for rasasv─Бda. Thus the worship of the Ayudhas removes the obstacles to, and prepares the way for, nididhyasana which is represented by the eighth Avarana.

192 ┼ЪRIVIDY─АSAPARY─АV─АSAN─А Eighth Avarana-Trikona (09-69) Nididhyasana should be performed to obtain the realisation of the identity with Paramatman with the help of the knowledge assured by manana. рдордирдиреЛрджрд┐рддрд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд╛рддреН рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдореИрдХреНрдпрд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрдпреЗ ред рдирд┐рджрд┐рдзреНрдпрд╛рд╕рдирд░реВрдкрдВ рд╣рд┐ рд╡рд┐рд╣рд┐рддрдВ рддрджреБрдкрд╛рд╕рдирдореН рее (Tatvasar─Бyaс╣Зa-Upasana Kanda) By Hence it can be safely inferred that nididhyasana is what this Avarana stands for. nididhyasana, the misconception “I do not perceive Siva” which is the effect of Abh─Бn─Бp─Бdakavarana, goes away. " рдХреГрддрд╢реНрд░рд╡рдгрдордирдирд╕реНрдп рдЕрдкрд░реЛрдХреНрд╖рд╛рддреНрдордЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдмрдиреНрдзрдХрд╛рднрд╛рдирд╛- рд╡реГрддрд┐рд░реВрдкрд╡рд┐рдкрд░реАрдд рднрд╛рд╡рдирд╛рдирд┐рд╡реГрддреНрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердВ рдирд┐рджрд┐рдзреНрдпрд╛рд╕рд╛ рдХрд░реНрддрд╡реНрдпрд╛. " Nididhyasana is the eradication of those modifications of the mind directed towards the objective world and the propagation of those towards the Atman. It is the fixing of the mind full of suddha satva steadily on the Atman as finally settled by manana. As samadhi is but the final stage of nididhyasana, wise men consider it as included in nididhyasana itself without treating it as a separate aid. The Sastras declare that the experience which is associated with the guddha triputi suggests nididhyasana and the KHANDA VI GIVI 193 experience рдЕрд╣рдВ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдорд╛рд╕реНрдорд┐ which is associated with a face-to-face realisation suggests the savikalpasamadhi. Nirvikalpasamadhi is that state where tripu╚Ыi is entirely absent. In nididhyasana the Atm─Бk─Бra vс╣Ыtti is brought about by an effort. It is likened to the forced bend of the branch of a tree that lasts only as long as the hands keep a hold on it; when the effort to hold it is removed, the bend disappears and the branch resumes its original shape. So too in nididhyasana when the effort to retain the Atmak─Бra vс╣Ыtti ceases, there is an instant return to anatm─Бk─Бravс╣Ыttis. Just as by repeated bending the branch retains the bend permanently, so also after repeated practice of nididhyasana the mind ceases to spring back to the repugnant an─Бtm─Бk─Бra ideas and remains ever as Atm─Бk─Бra. What the Brahmasutras mention in the following two sutras (IV. i. 1, 12) deserves to be noted in this connection. рдЖрд╡реГрддреНрддрд┐рд░рд╕рдХреГрджреБрдкрджреЗрд╢рд╛рддреН ред рдЖрдкреНрд░рд╛рдпрдгрд╛рддреН рддрддреНрд░рд╛рдкрд┐ рд╣рд┐ рджреГрд╖реНрдЯрдореН ред If nididhyasana should be successful, VasanaManon─Б┼Ыa and Tatvaj├▒ana should be This is the conclusion of kshaya, acquired simultaneously. the Sastras. ……… рд╡рд╛рд╕рдирд╛рдХреНрд╖рдпрд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдордиреЛрдирд╛рд╢рд╛ рдорд╣рд╛рдорддреЗ ред рд╕рдордХрд╛рд▓рдВ рдЪрд┐рд░рд╛рднреНрдпрд╕реНрддрд╛ рднрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ рдлрд▓рджрд╛ рдЗрдореЗ рее Ganito oivssendbet odajale (Annapurna Upd.) 13

194 ┼ЪR─кVIDYASAPARY─АV─АSAN─А Without Vasan─Бkshaya, Manon─Б┼Ыa does not accrue. Without Manon─Б┼Ыa, Tatvaj├▒ana does not arise and without Tatvaj├▒─Бna, V─Бsan─Бkshaya does not show its appearance. As these three are thus interdependent, they should all be practised simultaneously. By such a practice a direct realisation of the identity of Brahman and Atman arises immediately. Some Sastras however declare ┼Ъanti, Santosha and Vichara to be the chief aids to a direct realisation. Some great men likewise hold that Vairagya, Uparati and Bodha are essential. Being calculated to produce the same result-direct realisation, these three sets are to be considered identical in sense though differing verbally. As Jivabrahmaikya or the identity of Jiva and Brahman, which can be aptly called ‘Sarvasiddhi,’ is realised in this Chakra, it goes by the name of Sarvasiddhiprada Chakra. It is also appropriate that the Chitsakti that has this Chakra as its super-imposition should be called Atirahasyayoginis as it is associated with the pure Atm─Бk─Бra vс╣Ыtti which is the most superfine modification of the mind. The state of mind associated with nididhyasana transcends the sthula, s┼лkshma and k─Бraс╣Зa sariras and can fitly be called the turiya or fourth state, in which subsists the suddhasatvic feeling of

KHANDA VI 195 all-embracing oneness. The Chitsakti whereon it is super-imposed is known as Tripuramba (i.e., mother of the three puras) Chakre┼Ыvari. рд╡рд╛рдорд╛рджреАрдирд╛рдВ рдкреБрд░рд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рддреБ рдЬрдирдиреА рддреНрд░рд┐рдкреБрд░рд╛рдореНрдмрд┐рдХрд╛ | (Yoginihс╣Ыdaya. viii. 170) The firm conviction that before the creation of the universe made up of the Jagat, Jiva and Para, there was only the Chitsakti which is pure existence (рд╕рджреЗрд╡ рд╕реЛрдореНрдпреЗрджрдордЧреНрд░ рдЖрд╕реАрддреН ) and that it is only by its will that this universe came into being, arises only in the state of nididhyasana where all thoughts of anatman are entirely absent. Therefore it is that Ichcha (i. e., will) siddhi and Sarvabija (ie source of all) mudra are said to pervade this Chakra. Of the four Avaranadevat─Бs of this Chakra, Mah─Бk─Бmesvar─л represents V─Бsan─Бkshaya or extinction of latent impressions; Mah─Бvajre┼Ыvari, Manon─Б┼Ыa or dissolution of mind; Mahabhagam─Бlini, Tatvaj├▒─Бna or knowledge of reality; and Mah─Бtripurasundari, Brahm─Бtmaikya-aparokshaj├▒─Бna or the direct realisation of the identity of Atman and Brahman. 200 ┼ЪRIVIDYASAPARY─АV─АSANA Praptisiddhi is so called as it leads to the attainment of Brahman which is without attributes and beyond the turiya state. рддреБрд░реАрдпрд╛рддреАрддрдкрджрдкрд░рд╢рд┐рд╡рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрд┐рд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрд╛рдВ рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрд┐рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкрдпрддрд┐ рджрджрд╛рддреАрддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрд┐рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрд┐рдГ рее The Sarvayonimudr─Б represents that state where Brahmananda is felt as a result of the coa- lescence of ┼Ъiva and Sakti or the identity of Jiva and Brahman. As the Bindu is not in any way connected with trikona but stands detached, there seems to be sufficient reason to maintain that it represents only the sam─Бdhi known as Aspar┼Ыayoga or touchless Yoga mentioned in the Mandukya-K├дrik─Б. Turiyavidya. (2-3 Footnote) This represents the identity of Jiva and Brahman or the coalescence of Siva and Sakti which is experienced in savikalpasamadhi or turiya. vastha. It is what is also known as Mahapurti Vidya in Sastras. This is the ne plus ultra of Sri Vidya and is the state where even the all-pervading Vimar┼Ыa sakti merges into the Mahaprak─Б┼Ыa or the Supreme Effulgence. The realisation of non-duality is Sarvanandamayachakra. This is also the Mahodyanapitha.

HARKHANDA VI or рддрддрдГ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╛рдкрд░реЗ рд╡реНрдпреЛрдореНрдирд┐ рджреНрд╡рд╛рджрд╢рд╛рдиреНрддреЗрд╜рдЪреНрдпреБрддрд╛рддреНрдордХреЗ ред рдУрдбреНрдпрд╛рдкреАрдареЗ рдирд┐рд░реНрджреНрд╡рдиреНрджреНрд╡реЗ рдирд┐рд░рд╛рд▓рдореНрдмреЗ рдирд┐рд░рдЮреНрдЬрдиреЗ рее 201 (Yogasikhopanishad). This Turiyavidya represents what is at the background of the turiyatita (= beyond the fourth) state. It is the ┼Ыantyat─лtakala or the kala beyond santi. It is Parabrahman which is the coalescence of Prakasa and Vimar┼Ыa. It is Moksha, the highest form of Amс╣Ыta. It is the supreme matchless state which transcends and controls all mantras, all pithas or states of the mind, all yogas, all speech, all siddhis and all V─лras or J├▒─Бnis. It is also known as “sapekshika nirvikalpa samadhi.” The Sarvakamasiddhi and the Sarvatrikhandamudra pervade this Chakra. Sarvak─Бmasiddhi is that state where even the desire for the realisation of the identity of Atman and Brahman is absent. Sarvatrikhandamudra represents that state where the tripartite world (p. 106) appears in the partless self as a burnt cloth (the outline whereof is still visible in the charred remains) or a picture on a cinema screen. This suggests the state of a Jivanmukta. Here the Avarana portion of Aj├▒─Бna with its two aspects of asatv─Бp─Бdak─Бvarana and abh├вn─Гpadak─Бvarana has been removed by J├▒ana and Vikshepa alone remains. The illusory appearance of water in a desert continues by virtue of Badhi-

202 ┼ЪRIVIDYASAPARY─АV─АSAN─А t─Бnuvс╣Ыtti (i.e., continuance in spite of refutation) even after one knows full well that there is and can be no water there. As long as the Sun’s rays, sandy waste land and the eyes continue to exist, the appearance of the mirage at midday is inevi table. This is known as sop─Бdhikabhr─Бnti. The appearance of the world to a Jivanmukta is of thiskind. As long as he has a body, the world will continue to appear to him. But he will not cometo grief by this sensing of the world, because he does not re-act to the sensing. Nor does it entail a re-birth in his case. Grain that has been fried will only appease hunger but will not sprout when it is sown. The enjoyment of a Jivanmukta is of a similar nature. Thus the worship of the ninth Avarana represents savikalpasamadhi and the state of a Jivan. mukta. (ii) Pa├▒chapa├▒chik─Б P┼лj─Б. (28-29) The Paddhati says that above the Binduchakra the upasaka should imagine five stools piled oneover the other in the form of a throne and that in each of them, five deities should be worshipped. What these stand for is not however mentioned in any of the treatises dealing with vasanas. Therefore relying solely on the lotus feet of the Guru, an attempt is made here to suggest their significance. AMARAKHANDA VI divine 203 It is already stated that the Binduchakra represents savikalpasamadhi and as these five stools are said to be above the Binduchakra, it may safely be guessed that there should be five stages between savikalpasamadhi and nirvikalpasamadhi or sahajasthiti. Five such stages have been mentioned and explained at much length in the Tamil work on self-realisation self-realisation “Svanubhutirasayana” of Kodaganallur Sundarasvami, the great Brahmanishtha who flourished in South India in the last century (1831-1878). These five stages are in order Samya, Laya, Vin─Б┼Ыa, Atyantabhava and Aikya. (a) Samya is that state where the Jivopadhi (3) merges in the Akhandabrahmop─Бdhi (a) like water in milk, exhibiting only a semblance of the ┼Ыuddha-s┼лkshma-tripu╚Ыi. At Triveni in Prayag, although the dark waters of the Jumna and the crystal waters of the Ganges have united, the stream keeps on the dark colour for some distance; so it is in this samadhi. (b) Laya is that state where even the suddhas┼лkshmatriputi is merged and one entity aloneremains. (c) Vinasa is that state where the Akhandakara vс╣Ыtti or the Akhandopadhi disappears absolutely. Nivс╣Ыtti (disappearance) is of two kinds :layanivс╣Ыtti and n─Б┼Ыanivс╣Ыtti. e.g. the disappearance-

204 ┼ЪRIVIDYASAPARY─АV─АSAN─А of the world in deep sleep and in the turiya state respectively. In (b) above, there is only layanivс╣Ыtti of the Akhandopadhi, while here there is its n─Б┼Ыanivс╣Ыtti. (d) Atyant─Бbh─Бva is that state wherein there is the realisation of the non-existence at any time of differences in consciousness as the Jiva consciousness, Brahman consciousness or Akhanda or allpervading consciousness, apart from svabhava sthiti (natural condition), such differences being only contingent, not absolute. (e) Aikya. Some books on practical realisation. call this also At─лtodita (inexpressible) or An─Бm─Бkhya (nameless); for it will not be right to call it even as Bodh─Бt─лta. It is difficult even to conceive of this and still more to describe it as such and such. The above is one way of explaining the Pa├▒chapa├▒chikas. = Kuladipa. (3) Kula triputi (knower, known and knowledge) and Dipa J├▒ana or Chetana. The appearance of triputi is due to illusory differences super-imposed on the pure Chetana. Triputi is of two kinds :bahya or external, and antara or internal, according as it relates to the gross or the subtle world. Both are the outcome of Avidya and are in consequence impure. рдЕрдиреНрддрд╕реНрддреЗрдЬреЛ рдмрд╣рд┐рд╕реНрддреЗрдЬ рдПрдХреАрдХреГрддреНрдпрд╛рдорд┐рддрдкреНрд░рднрдореН ред рддреНрд░рд┐рдзрд╛ рджреАрдкрдВ рдкрд░рд┐рднреНрд░рд╛рдореНрдп рдХреБрд▓рджреАрдкрдВ рдирд┐рд╡реЗрджрдпреЗ || The above verse recited in offering the Kuladipa means:-“Uniting the J├▒ana at the background of the antaratriputi with that at the background of the bahyatripu╚Ыi, and revolving the dipa of immeasureable brilliance thrice, I offer this Kuladipa.” The identification of the two triputis is possible only by looking at their substratum. The upasaka should contemplate on this unbroken brilliance thrice and in the end dedicate even this contemplation, which is virtually Akhandakaravс╣Ыtti, to the Mahaprak─Б┼Ыa or Supreme Effulgence, i.e., merge it therein. It should be understood that the first contemplation is to get over the impure bahyatripu╚Ыi, the next to eliminate the impure antaratriputi and the last to remove even the pure tripu╚Ыi. 214 ┼ЪRIVIDYASAPARY─АV─АSAN─А leaving no remnant behind, so also the variegated world of names and forms disappears with its rootwhen the light of Akhand─Бk─Бravс╣Ыtti is applied to it. Mantrapushpa. (ss) Mantrapushpa or consecrated pushpa├▒jali is the offering of a handful of flowers, which are of the form of mantras, to the Paradevat─Б. Mantra means “that which liberates from the ocean of sorrow those who meditate on it.” ga gf├а. KHANDA VII K─Бmakal─Бdhy─Бna (103-10). This Khanda treats exclusively of K─Бmakal─Б and its contemplation. Kamakala is the samarasya. of Siva and Sakti, or what is known in the Vedanta as Jivabrahmaikya. It is represented in two forms and its contemplation is likewise twofold. . рд▓рд╛. CC-0S.P. Dhar Collection. Digitized by eGangotri KHANDA VIII. Homa (резрежрек,резрезрел тАУ резрейреи) This Khanda with its Appendix lays down the elaborate ritual pertaining to Homa, but adds that the ceremonial may be gone through or omitted altogether according to convenience, its performance no doubt conferring merit, its omission involving however no sin. tyo The word, from the root to sacrifice, means an offering or gift of what is in one’s possession, but is restricted in application to oblations to gods offered into the consecrated fire. Though such bahya or external Homa is declared to be optional, its metaphysical aspect or the antara (internal) Homa cannot be ignored but should be well understood and it is accordingly dealt with here in some detail. The Paddhati at the outset requires that the altar for the Homa should be provided in the north-east of the chamber of worship. What is the significance of specifying the north-east for this purpose? The following evidently supplies the clue. It is a settled conclusion of the Upanishads KHANDA VIII 223 that the Sahasrara in the Chitchandramandala is a lotus of eight large-size petals pointing in the eight directions, with one hundred and twenty-five smaller petals in each, that in the pericarp of the lotus is the “hamsa” or the Jiv─Бtman and that he moves in the eight petals etc., with varying modifications of the mind. In describing these modifications, the Hamsopanishad says that in thenorth-east petal, the Jiv─Бtman is permeated by a desire for making gifts and renouncing possessions.. рддрд╕реНрдпрд╛рд╖реНрдЯрдзрд╛ рд╡реГрддреНрддрд┐рд░реНрднрд╡рддрд┐, рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рджрд│реЗ рдкреБрдгреНрдпреЗ рдорддрд┐рдГ рдИрд╢рд╛рдиреНрдпреЗ рджреНрд░рд╡реНрдпрджрд╛рдирдВ рддреНрдпрд╛рдЧрдмреБрджреНрдзрд┐рд╢реНрд╡, рдордзреНрдпреЗ рд╡реИрд░рд╛рдЧреНрдпрдВ ред

The Naradaparivrajakopanishad however says that in that quarter, tatvaj├▒ana or knowledge of thereality arises. рдкреНрд░рд╛рдЧреНрджрд▓реЗ рдкреБрдгреНрдпрд╡реГрддреНрддрд┐рдГ * * * рдИрд╢рд╛рдиреНрдпреЗ рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдВ, рдХрд░реНрдгрд┐рдХрд╛рдпрд╛рдВ рд╡реИрд░рд╛рдЧреНрдпрдВ, рдХреЗрд╕рд░реЗрд╖реНрд╡рд╛рддреНрдордЪрд┐рдиреНрддрд╛. Both mean practically the same thing; for is not the renunciation of attachment to the super-impositions the knowledge of the substratum? The chamber of worship representing, as it does, the pure mind (p. 45), it is. only appropriate that its north-east, which is associated with renunciation, should have been prescribed for Homa. What is it that should be sacrificed? Not only all that one possesses but also the egotistic idea of one’s ownership of them, or in other words the

224 ┼ЪRIVIDYASAPARY─АV─АSAN─А Ahanta and Mamata i.e., the feelings of “I” and “mine”. This is the conclusion of the J├▒ana┼Ы─Бstras. Why? Because both of them are only illusory creations (adhy─Бropa) of Avidya on the Atman, ahanta being the feeling of “I” in regard to the three bodies and the five sheaths which are not the self and mamata, the feeling of “mine” in respect of internal and external objects not really pertaining to the self. It is these feelings of “I” and “mine” that constitute bondage and they should therefore be sacrificed in the fire of knowledge. рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд╛рдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдХрд░реНрдорд╛рдгрд┐ рднрд╕реНрдорд╕рд╛рддреНрдХреБрд░реБрддреЗ рддрдерд╛ ред (Gita. iv. 37 ) The following text of J├▒─Бn─Бrс╣Зava also deserves to be noticed in this connection. рдкрд░рд╛рд╣рдВрддрд╛рдордпреЗ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирджреАрдкрд╡рд┐рдЬреГрдореНрднрд┐реСрддреЗ ред рд╕рдВрд╡рд┐рджрдиреНрдиреМ рд╣реБрдиреЗрджреЗрд╡рд┐ рдкреНрд░рдкрдЮреНрдЪрд╣рд╡рд┐рд░реБрддреНрдХрдЯрдореН рее According to it it is the universe that is ├бehoblation to be thrown into the fire of Parahantt or Atman, J├▒anavasishс╣нha and other authori tative works declare that the mind with sankalpas and vikalpas is the universe. Balidana is the offering of an object to a devat─Б. In this sense, naivedya dealt with in Khanda VI will also be bali; but it is not usual to call it so. as рдЕрддрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рддрджреНрдмреБрджреНрдзрд┐рдВ рдЬрдирдпрд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛ рдЙрдиреНрдорд╛рд░реНрдЧрдкреНрд░рд╡рд░реНрддрд┐рдХрд╛рдГ рд╢рдХреНрддрдпрдГ i.e, those Saktis that lead one astray by inducing erroneous knowledge. Erroneous knowledge or adhy─Бsa as it is called is of two kinds-nirup─Бdhika and sopadhika-common examples whereof the perception of a serpent in a rope and the appearance of water in a sandy waste respectively. The sakti that gives rise to such erroneous perceptions and their concomitants, fear, joy etc. is known as Maya or Aj├▒─Бna, and it is to this bh┼лta that the balid─Бna has to be made.

230 ┼ЪRIVIDYASAPARYAVASAN─А For the removal of such malefic influences a prayer was no doubt sent forth at the very outset (p.78) that they “might perish by the command of ┼Ъiva”. But whatever the strength of feeling behind that prayer, they keep on appearing again and again by Badhitanuvс╣Ыtti (explained on p. 202) as in the case of the mirage. It is necessary to note that the persistence of such erroneous perception even after the knowledge of the background! is due to the upadhi alone. The appearance of the universe to a Jivanmukta is due to upadhi. Just as for the mirage, the Sun’s rays, the sand, the eyes of the beholder etc., are the upadhis, so also for the appearance of the universe to a Jivanmukta, his body is the upadhi. This body continues: to exist till his prarabdha is worked off. “Does not prarabdha cease for a Jivanmukta?” is a legitimate question. True; for a Juani there is no prarabdha. The moment the adhyasa of “I” on his body ceased on attaining tatvaj├▒─Бna, his prarabdha karma also had died out. рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд╛рдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдХрд░реНрдорд╛рдгрд┐ рднрд╕реНрдорд╕рд╛рддреНрдХреБрд░реБрддреЗ рддрдерд╛ ред says the G─лt─Б (iv. 37). But in the eyes of others it appears as if there is a portion of prarabdha still left over. According to the Manishapa├▒chaka text quoted on p.128, the J├▒ani makes over his body to pr─Бrabdha. Therefore, the body alone is the remnant of his pr├дrabdha and as it has been accepted that the body is the upadhi for the appearance of

KHANDA IX 231 the universe, such appearance is bound to persist as long as the body exists. But the appearance of the universe that was formerly an obstacle to his attainment of J├▒ana is really no impediment after his attaining J├▒ana. The appearance is caused by vikshepa┼Ыakti.. Aj├▒─Бna has, as already stated on p. 88, two ┼Ыaktis: -avarana and vikshepa. It is only vikshepa associated with avarana that brings about bondage. Vikshepa alone without avarana is incapable of producing bondage. To a Jivanmukta the appearance of the world is due to vikshepa unassociated with avarana; for has not avarana been destroyed already by Atmaj├▒─Бna? For the appearance of the world and for the body which is the upadhi Therefore therefor, the mind alone is the cause. the mind alone is the bhuta and balid─Бna is madeto satisfy it. This is a great secret. The Paddhati says " рдмрд▓рд┐рдкрд╛рддреНрд░реЗ рдирд┐рд╡реЗрджрдирд╕рд╛рдордЧреНрд░реАрдГ рдХрд┐рдВрдЪрд┐fa.” It therefore appears that the aj├▒─Бn─Бm┼Ыas, i.e., nama and r┼лpa, of the articles offered as naivedya to the devata are alone meant for balid─Бna. 232 SRIVIDYASAPARY─АV─АSAN─А The Akhandakaravс╣Ыtti is the Vyapakamaс╣Зdala on which the bali is offered. Having eliminated name and form by the two syllables a and, the prak─Б┼Ыa and vimar┼Ыa pranavas, the up─Бsaka should offer them to the obstructing bh┼лtas and drive these far away. The particles indicate the act of driving. After balid─Бna in this manner, the Paddhati lays down Pradakshina, Namaskara and Japa. Pradakshina: The significance of pradakshina is the elimination of the gross or jada aspect i.e., name and form of the objects of sense which the mind in its various modifications tries to reach and merging them in Brahman. Namask─Бra is remaining as Brahman without the slightest trace of names and forms. Japa can be classed under three heads-ni- gada, upam┼Ыu and manasika. Nigada is pro- nouncing the mantra aloud, up─Бmsu is to pronounce it in such a way that it is audible only to oneself and manasika is mental contemplation. Of these it is the manasika alone that is said to be prescribed for the uttam─Бdhik─Бris. KHANDA X. P┼лj─Бsamarpaс╣Зa and Devatodv─Бsana. (992) Paj─Бsamarpana:-That the puja is nididhyasana and savikalpasamadhi has been mentioned clearly in the Introduction and re-iterated several times in the course of the succeeding Khandas. Nididhyasana and Savikalpasamadhi are of the nature of steady contemplation of Jivabrahmaikya and are Akhaс╣Зс╕Н─Бk─Бravс╣Ыtti. This Akhandakaravс╣Ыtti is Vimarsa. This is also what is known as Vс╣Ыttij├▒─Бna. This should be dedicated to the Paradevata i.e., merged in Her. After the eradication of the knot of the heart, doubts and karmas, no purpose is served by nididhyasana and savikalpasamadhi or in other words Akhaс╣Зс╕Н─Бk─Бravс╣Ыtti. Therefore Vimar┼Ыaj├▒─Бna or the suddha triputi also disappears. and the pure j├▒eya, Brahman, alone remains. KHANDA XI. S├дntistava and Visesh├дrghyodv─Бsana. (113). Santistava The word means nityatс╣Ыpti or eternal satisfaction. This is had when all desires. are attained. According to the text “sag i " of the Taittiriya Upanishad, it is the Atmaj├▒─Бni alone that can be said to have attained all his desires. with his work. He He alone is kс╣Ыtakrty a or done Therefore he has neither pravс╣Ыtti nor nivrtti. He has nothing else still to do. can be compared to the tranquil waveless ocean. This state is termed Santi. A J├▒─Бni who has reached this state, by virtue of his innate qualities of Maitri, karun─Б etc., wishes that the whole world should reach to the eminence he has attained and sends out his prayer to Parame┼Ыvara asking him to bestow His рд▓реЛрдХрд╛рдГ рд╕рдорд╕реНрддрд╛рдГ рд╕реБрдЦрд┐рдиреЛ рднрд╡рдиреНрддреБ in common usage. IV that the Visesharghya is the YatharthaviseVisesharghyodvasana:-It was said in Khanda shaj├▒─Бna. This J├▒ana will arise only in a pure mind. The realisation тАЬрд╕рд░реНрд╡рдВ рдЦрд▓реНрд╡рд┐рджрдВ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдо” тАЬрдЕрд╣рдВ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдорд╛рд╕реНрдорд┐” arises only in the Akhandakaravс╣Ыtti which is within the reach of a mind predominant in

244 ┼ЪR─кVIDY ASAPARY─АV─АSAN─А suddhasatva. This state is called Turiya. Savikalpasamadhi is also the same. Nirvikalpasam─Бdhi is that state where the suddha triputi existing in the savikalpa state disappears and the mind merges in the secondless ┼Ъiva. This is also of two kinds: advaitabhavana and advaitavasthana. When the nirvikalpasamadhi is associated with the aj├▒─Бtavс╣Ыtti of the antahkarana, it is the advaitabh─Бvan─Б kind. P┼лj─Бsamarpana and devatodv─Бsana come under this class. When practice in this gets deeper and deeper, the Sivakaravс╣Ыtti also settles down. This state that is without any vс╣Ыtti is known as the upa┼Ы─Бnta state or advaitavasth─Бna nirvikalpasam─Бdhi. Just as a drop of water sprinkled on a red-hot bar of iron merges into the iron, so also in this state the sivakara chitvс╣Ыtti, which is Vimar┼Ыa, merges in the Siva who is Mahaprak─Б┼Ыa. This in the opinion of the great is the tatva of the Visesharghyodvasana. It is in this state that Santistava finds a place. рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдореИрд╡рд╛рд╣рдВ рдЪрд┐рджреЗрд╡рд╛рд╣рдореЗрд╡рдВ рд╡рд╛рдкрд┐ рди рдЪрд┐рдиреНрддреНрдпрддреЗ ред рдЪрд┐рдиреНрдорд╛рддреНрд░реЗрдгреИрд╡ рдпрд╕реНрддрд┐рд╖реНрдареЗрддреН рд╡реИрджреЗрд╣реАрдореБрдХреНрдд рдПрд╡ рд╕рдГ ред рдирд┐рд╢реНрдЪрдпрдВ рдЪ рдкрд░рд┐рддреНрдпрдЬреНрдпрд╛рд╣рдВ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдорд╛рд╕реНрдореАрддрд┐ рдирд┐рд╢реНрдЪрдпрдореН ред рдЖрдирдиреНрджрднрд░рд┐рддрд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдиреНрддреЛ рд╡реИрджреЗрд╣реАрдореБрдХреНрдд рдПрд╡ рд╕рдГ || (Tejobindu Upanishad).
